# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Implementation

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement RBAC authorization. Identify: the RBACAuthorizer with its Authorize method (in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/), the SubjectAccessEvaluator, the DefaultRuleResolver that resolves PolicyRules for a user, the SubjectAccessReview REST handler, the bootstrap RBAC policy definitions, and the policy-based storage for Role and ClusterRoleBinding objects with escalation prevention.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

76-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Go source files implementing RBAC authorization in kubernetes/kubernetes. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified:

1. **RBACAuthorizer** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`) - The main authorization engine with the `Authorize` method that evaluates access requests based on RBAC rules.

2. **SubjectAccessEvaluator** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go`) - Determines which subjects are allowed to perform specific actions using the `AllowedSubjects` method.

3. **DefaultRuleResolver** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`) - Resolves PolicyRules for users by examining RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings, providing `RulesFor`, `VisitRulesFor`, and `GetRoleReferenceRules` methods.

4. **SubjectAccessReview REST Handler** (`pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go`) - Handles the SubjectAccessReview API requests with the `Create` method.

5. **Bootstrap RBAC Policies** - Defined in `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/`:
   - `policy.go` - Cluster-wide roles and bindings
   - `controller_policy.go` - Controller component roles
   - `namespace_policy.go` - Namespace-scoped roles

6. **Policy-Based Storage with Escalation Prevention**:
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go` - Role storage with checks
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go` - ClusterRole storage
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go` - RoleBinding storage
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go` - ClusterRoleBinding storage
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go` - Escalation prevention functions

Kubernetes RBAC authorization system is comprehensively implemented across multiple Go source files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. Here are the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\n**RBACAuthorizer** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go) - The main authorizer implementing the authorizer.Authorizer interface. It contains the Authorize method that evaluates whether a request should be allowed based on RBAC rules. The authorizer uses a RequestToRuleMapper interface to resolve policy rules for users and namespaces. It implements a visitor pattern through authorizingVisitor to evaluate rules against request attributes.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution and Policy Evaluation\\n\\n**DefaultRuleResolver** (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go) - Implements comprehensive rule resolution for RBAC. It provides:\\n- RulesFor() method that accumulates all applicable policy rules for a user in a namespace\\n- VisitRulesFor() method that iterates through all applicable rules by visiting cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules() method that resolves Role or ClusterRole references from RoleBindings/ClusterRoleBindings\\n- Supports matching users against various subject types (Users, Groups, ServiceAccounts)\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\n**SubjectAccessEvaluator** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go) - Implements the SubjectLocator interface to determine which subjects are allowed to perform specific actions. The AllowedSubjects() method returns all subjects (users, groups, service accounts) that can perform a given action by examining applicable RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings.\\n\\n## REST API Handler\\n\\n**SubjectAccessReview REST Handler** (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go) - Handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. The REST struct with Create() method evaluates whether a user can perform an action and returns the decision status. It converts SubjectAccessReview specifications into authorization attributes and delegates to the authorizer for evaluation.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policy definitions are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/:\\n- **policy.go** - Defines cluster-wide roles and role bindings including system roles (cluster-admin, system:nodes, etc.) and component roles (kube-controller-manager, kube-scheduler, etc.)\\n- **controller_policy.go** - Defines roles for Kubernetes controllers (replication controller manager, daemon set controller, etc.)\\n- **namespace_policy.go** - Defines namespace-scoped roles for system namespaces\\n\\nThese bootstrap policies are reconciled with the cluster in **pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go** through the EnsureRBACPolicy() function which creates or updates bootstrap roles and role bindings.\\n\\n## Privilege Escalation Prevention\\n\\nPrivilege escalation is prevented through multiple policy-based storage implementations:\\n\\n**Role Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go) - Wraps the standard storage for Roles with escalation checks. Create and Update methods verify that users cannot create/modify roles with permissions they don't already possess.\\n\\n**ClusterRole Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go) - Similar escalation prevention for ClusterRoles with additional checks for aggregation rules which require cluster-admin privileges.\\n\\n**RoleBinding Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go) - Prevents users from binding roles they're not authorized to use by verifying users have the \\\"bind\\\" privilege on the target role.\\n\\n**ClusterRoleBinding Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go) - Cluster-wide equivalent of role binding privilege escalation prevention.\\n\\n**Escalation Check Functions** (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go) - Provides utility functions:\\n- EscalationAllowed() - Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() - Verifies user has explicit \\\"escalate\\\" permission on roles\\n- BindingAuthorized() - Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" permission for the referenced role\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() - Core validation that ensures user doesn't grant permissions they don't possess\\n\\nThe escalation prevention is implemented by having the policy-based storage layers call ConfirmNoEscalation() through the AuthorizationRuleResolver, comparing rules the user is trying to create against the rules they currently possess, denying creation if it would escalate privileges.\"\n}\n",

Kubernetes RBAC authorization system is comprehensively implemented across multiple Go source files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. Here are the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\n**RBACAuthorizer** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go) - The main authorizer implementing the authorizer.Authorizer interface. It contains the Authorize method that evaluates whether a request should be allowed based on RBAC rules. The authorizer uses a RequestToRuleMapper interface to resolve policy rules for users and namespaces. It implements a visitor pattern through authorizingVisitor to evaluate rules against request attributes.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution and Policy Evaluation\\n\\n**DefaultRuleResolver** (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go) - Implements comprehensive rule resolution for RBAC. It provides:\\n- RulesFor() method that accumulates all applicable policy rules for a user in a namespace\\n- VisitRulesFor() method that iterates through all applicable rules by visiting cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules() method that resolves Role or ClusterRole references from RoleBindings/ClusterRoleBindings\\n- Supports matching users against various subject types (Users, Groups, ServiceAccounts)\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\n**SubjectAccessEvaluator** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go) - Implements the SubjectLocator interface to determine which subjects are allowed to perform specific actions. The AllowedSubjects() method returns all subjects (users, groups, service accounts) that can perform a given action by examining applicable RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings.\\n\\n## REST API Handler\\n\\n**SubjectAccessReview REST Handler** (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go) - Handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. The REST struct with Create() method evaluates whether a user can perform an action and returns the decision status. It converts SubjectAccessReview specifications into authorization attributes and delegates to the authorizer for evaluation.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policy definitions are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/:\\n- **policy.go** - Defines cluster-wide roles and role bindings including system roles (cluster-admin, system:nodes, etc.) and component roles (kube-controller-manager, kube-scheduler, etc.)\\n- **controller_policy.go** - Defines roles for Kubernetes controllers (replication controller manager, daemon set controller, etc.)\\n- **namespace_policy.go** - Defines namespace-scoped roles for system namespaces\\n\\nThese bootstrap policies are reconciled with the cluster in **pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go** through the EnsureRBACPolicy() function which creates or updates bootstrap roles and role bindings.\\n\\n## Privilege Escalation Prevention\\n\\nPrivilege escalation is prevented through multiple policy-based storage implementations:\\n\\n**Role Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go) - Wraps the standard storage for Roles with escalation checks. Create and Update methods verify that users cannot create/modify roles with permissions they don't already possess.\\n\\n**ClusterRole Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go) - Similar escalation prevention for ClusterRoles with additional checks for aggregation rules which require cluster-admin privileges.\\n\\n**RoleBinding Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go) - Prevents users from binding roles they're not authorized to use by verifying users have the \\\"bind\\\" privilege on the target role.\\n\\n**ClusterRoleBinding Storage** (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go) - Cluster-wide equivalent of role binding privilege escalation prevention.\\n\\n**Escalation Check Functions** (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go) - Provides utility functions:\\n- EscalationAllowed() - Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() - Verifies user has explicit \\\"escalate\\\" permission on roles\\n- BindingAuthorized() - Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" permission for the referenced role\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() - Core validation that ensures user doesn't grant permissions they don't possess\\n\\nThe escalation prevention is implemented by having the policy-based storage layers call ConfirmNoEscalation() through the AuthorizationRuleResolver, comparing rules the user is trying to create against the rules they currently possess, denying creation if it would escalate privileges.\"\n}\n",
